of the world\n</td>\n<td>4,110\n</td>\n<td>12%\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Total\n</td>\n<td>34,011\n</td>\n<td>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Professional_golf">Professional golf</span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Professional_golfer" title="Professional golfer">Professional golfer</a></div>\n<p>The majority of <a href="/wiki/Professional_golfer" title="Professional golfer">professional golfers</a> work as club or teaching professionals ("pros"), and only compete in local competitions. A small elite of professional golfers are "tournament pros" who compete full-time on international "tours". Many club and teaching professionals working in the golf industry start as <a href="/wiki/Caddies" class="mw-redirect" title="Caddies">caddies</a> or with a general interest in the game, finding employment at <a href="/wiki/Golf_course" title="Golf course">golf courses</a> and eventually moving on to certifications in their chosen profession. These programs include independent institutions and universities, and those that eventually lead to a Class A golf professional certification. Touring professionals typically start as amateur players, who attain their "pro" status after success in major tournaments that win them either prize money and/or notice from corporate sponsors. <a href="/wiki/Jack_Nicklaus" title="Jack Nicklaus">Jack Nicklaus</a>, for example, gained widespread notice by finishing second in the 1960 <a href="/wiki/U.S._Open_(golf)" title="U.S. Open (golf)">U.S. Open</a> to champion <a href="/wiki/Arnold_Palmer" title="Arnold Palmer">Arnold Palmer</a>, with a 72-hole score of 282 (the best score to date in that tournament by an amateur). He played one more amateur year in 1961, winning that year\'s <a href="/wiki/United_States_Amateur_Championship_(golf)" title="United States Amateur Championship (golf)">U.S. Amateur Championship</a>, before turning pro in 1962.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Instruction">Instruction</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Indoor_Putting_Green.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Indoor_Putting_Green.JPG/170px-Indoor_Putting_Green.JPG" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Indoor_Putting_Green.JPG/255px-Indoor_Putting_Green.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Indoor_Putting_Green.JPG/340px-Indoor_Putting_Green.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1224" data-file-height="1632" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Indoor_Putting_Green.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Indoor <a href="/wiki/Golf_course#Putting_green" title="Golf course">putting green</a> for practice and instruction</div></div></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Golf_instruction" title="Golf instruction">Golf instruction</a></div>\n<p>Golf instruction involves the teaching and learning of the game of golf. Proficiency in teaching golf instruction requires not only technical and physical ability but also knowledge of the rules and etiquette of the game. In some countries, golf instruction is best performed by teachers certified by the <a href="/wiki/Professional_Golfers_Association" title="Professional Golfers Association">Professional Golfers Association</a>. Some top instructors who work with professional golfers have become quite well known in their own right. Professional golf instructors can use physical conditioning, mental visualization, classroom sessions, club fitting, driving range instruction, on-course play under real conditions, and review of videotaped swings in slow motion to teach golf to prepare the golfer for the course.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Golf_tours">Golf tours</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Professional_golf_tours" title="Professional golf tours">Professional golf tours</a></div>\n<p>There are at least twenty professional golf tours, each run by a <a href="/wiki/Professional_Golfers_Association" title="Professional Golfers Association">PGA</a> or an independent tour organization, which is responsible for arranging events, finding sponsors, and regulating the tour. Typically a tour has "members" who are entitled to compete in most of its events, and also invites non-members to compete in some of them. Gaining membership of an elite tour is highly competitive, and most professional golfers never achieve it.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:All_Black.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/All_Black.jpg/170px-All_Black.jpg" width="170" height="167" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/All_Black.jpg/255px-All_Black.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/All_Black.jpg/340px-All_Black.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1500" data-file-height="1475" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:All_Black.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Gary_Player" title="Gary Player">Gary Player</a> is widely regarded as one of the greatest players in the history of golf.</div></div></div>\n<p>Perhaps the most widely known tour is the <a href="/wiki/PGA_Tour" title="PGA Tour">PGA Tour</a>, which tends to attract the strongest fields, outside the four Majors and the four World Golf Championships events. This is due mostly to the fact that most PGA Tour events have a first prize of at least 800,000 <a href="/wiki/USD" class="mw-redirect" title="USD">USD</a>. The <a href="/wiki/PGA_European_Tour" title="PGA European Tour">European Tour</a>, which attracts a substantial number of top golfers from outside North America, ranks second to the PGA Tour in worldwide prestige. Some top professionals from outside North America play enough tournaments to maintain membership on both the PGA Tour and European Tour. Since 2010, both tours\' money titles have been claimed by the same individual three times, with <a href="/wiki/Luke_Donald" title="Luke Donald">Luke Donald</a> doing so in 2011 and <a href="/wiki/Rory_McIlroy" title="Rory McIlroy">Rory McIlroy</a> in 2012 and 2014. In 2013, <a href="/wiki/Henrik_Stenson" title="Henrik Stenson">Henrik Stenson</a> won the <a href="/wiki/FedEx_Cup" title="FedEx Cup">FedEx Cup</a> points race on the PGA Tour and the European Tour money title, but did not top the PGA Tour money list (that honour going to <a href="/wiki/Tiger_Woods" title="Tiger Woods">Tiger Woods</a>).\n</p><p>The other leading men\'s tours include the <a href="/wiki/Japan_Golf_Tour" title="Japan Golf Tour">Japan Golf Tour</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Asian_Tour" title="Asian Tour">Asian Tour</a> (Asia outside Japan), the <a href="/wiki/PGA_Tour_of_Australasia" title="PGA Tour of Australasia">PGA Tour of Australasia</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Sunshine_Tour" title="Sunshine Tour">Sunshine Tour</a> (for southern Africa, primarily South Africa). The Japan, Australasian, Sunshine, PGA, and European Tours are the charter members of the trade body of the world\'s main tours, the International Federation of PGA Tours, founded in 1996. The Asian Tour became a full member in 1999. The <a href="/wiki/PGA_Tour_Canada" title="PGA Tour Canada">Canadian Tour</a> became an associate member of the Federation in 2000, and the <a href="/wiki/Tour_de_las_Am%C3%A9ricas" title="Tour de las Am\xc3\xa9ricas">Tour de las Am\xc3\xa9ricas</a> (Latin America) became an associate member of the Federation in 2007. The Federation underwent a major expansion in 2009 that saw eleven new tours become full members&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 the Canadian Tour, Tour de las Am\xc3\xa9ricas, China Golf Association, the Korea Professional Golfers\' Association, <a href="/wiki/Professional_Golf_Tour_of_India" title="Professional Golf Tour of India">Professional Golf Tour of India</a>, and the operators of all six major women\'s tours worldwide. The <a href="/wiki/OneAsia_Tour" class="mw-redirect" title="OneAsia Tour">OneAsia Tour</a>, founded in 2009, is not a member of the Federation, but was founded as a joint venture of the Australasia, China, Japan, and Korean tours. In 2011, the Tour de las Am\xc3\xa9ricas was effectively taken over by the PGA Tour, and in 2012 was folded into the new <a href="/wiki/PGA_Tour_Latinoam%C3%A9rica" title="PGA Tour Latinoam\xc3\xa9rica">PGA Tour Latinoam\xc3\xa9rica</a>. Also in 2012, the Canadian Tour was renamed <a href="/wiki/PGA_Tour_Canada" title="PGA Tour Canada">PGA Tour Canada</a> after it agreed to be taken over by the PGA Tour. All men\'s tours that are Federation members, except the India tour, offer points in the <a href="/wiki/Official_World_Golf_Ranking" title="Official World Golf Ranking">Official World Golf Ranking</a> (OWGR) to players who place sufficiently high in their events. The OneAsia Tour also offers ranking points.\n</p><p>Golf is unique in having lucrative competition for older players. There are several senior tours for men aged fifty and over, arguably the best known of which is the U.S.-based <a href="/wiki/PGA_Tour_Champions" title="PGA Tour Champions">PGA Tour Champions</a>.\n</p><p>There are six principal tours for women, each based in a different country or continent. The most prestigious of these is the United States-based <a href="/wiki/LPGA" title="LPGA">LPGA Tour</a>. All of the principal tours offer points in the <a href="/wiki/Women%27s_World_Golf_Rankings" title="Women&#39;s World Golf Rankings">Women\'s World Golf Rankings</a> for high finishers in their events.\n</p><p>All of the leading professional tours for under-50 players have an official developmental tour, in which the leading players at the end of the season will earn a tour card on the main tour for the following season. Examples include the <a href="/wiki/Web.com_Tour" title="Web.com Tour">Web.com Tour</a>, which feeds to the PGA Tour, and the <a href="/wiki/Challenge_Tour" title="Challenge Tour">Challenge Tour</a>, which is the developmental tour of the European Tour. The Web.com and Challenge Tours also offer OWGR points.\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Men.27s_major_championships"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Men\'s_major_championships">Men\'s major championships</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Lee_Westwood_bunker.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Lee_Westwood_bunker.jpg/220px-Lee_Westwood_bunker.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Lee_Westwood_bunker.jpg/330px-Lee_Westwood_bunker.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Lee_Westwood_bunker.jpg/440px-Lee_Westwood_bunker.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3456" data-file-height="2304" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Lee_Westwood_bunker.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Lee_Westwood" title="Lee Westwood">Lee Westwood</a> pictured making a bunker shot at the <a href="/wiki/2008_Open_Championship" title="2008 Open Championship">2008 Open</a></div></div></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Men%27s_major_golf_championships" title="Men&#39;s major golf championships">Men\'s major golf championships</a></div>\n<p>The major championships are the four most prestigious men\'s tournaments of the year. In chronological order they are: <a href="/wiki/Masters_Tournament" title="Masters Tournament">The Masters</a>, the <a href="/wiki/U.S._Open_(golf)" title="U.S. Open (golf)">U.S. Open</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Open_Championship" title="The Open Championship">The Open Championship</a> (referred to in North America as the British Open) and the <a href="/wiki/PGA_Championship" title="PGA Championship">PGA Championship</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The fields for these events include the top several dozen golfers from all over the world. The Masters has been played at <a href="/wiki/Augusta_National_Golf_Club" title="Augusta National Golf Club">Augusta National Golf Club</a> in Augusta, Georgia, since its inception in 1934. It is the only major championship that is played at the same course each year.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> The U.S. Open and PGA Championship are played at courses around the United States, while the Open Championship is played at courses around the United Kingdom.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Prior to the advent of the PGA Championship and The Masters, the four Majors were the U.S. Open, the U.S. Amateur, the Open Championship, and the <a href="/wiki/The_Amateur_Championship" title="The Amateur Championship">British Amateur</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Women.27s_major_championships"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Women\'s_major_championships">Women\'s major championships</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:2007_LPGA_Championship_-_Lorena_Ochoa_(1).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/2007_LPGA_Championship_-_Lorena_Ochoa_%281%29.jpg/170px-2007_LPGA_Championship_-_Lorena_Ochoa_%281%29.jpg" width="170" height="236" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/2007_LPGA_Championship_-_Lorena_Ochoa_%281%29.jpg/255px-2007_LPGA_Championship_-_Lorena_Ochoa_%281%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/2007_LPGA_Championship_-_Lorena_Ochoa_%281%29.jpg/340px-2007_LPGA_Championship_-_Lorena_Ochoa_%281%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2095" data-file-height="2907" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:2007_LPGA_Championship_-_Lorena_Ochoa_(1).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Lorena_Ochoa" title="Lorena Ochoa">Lorena Ochoa</a>, a retired number one female golfer, pictured here in 2007</div></div></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Women%27s_major_golf_championships" title="Women&#39;s major golf championships">Women\'s major golf championships</a></div>\n<p>Women\'s golf does not have a globally agreed set of majors. The list of majors recognised by the dominant women\'s tour, the <a href="/wiki/LPGA" title="LPGA">LPGA Tour</a> in the U.S., has changed several times over the years, with the most recent changes occurring in 2001 and 2013. Like the PGA Tour, the (U.S.) LPGA<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> tour long had four majors, but now has five: the <a href="/wiki/ANA_Inspiration" title="ANA Inspiration">ANA Inspiration</a> (previously known by several other names, most recently the Kraft Nabisco Championship), the <a href="/wiki/Women%27s_PGA_Championship" title="Women&#39;s PGA Championship">Women\'s PGA Championship</a> (previously known as the LPGA Championship),<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Women%27s_Open_Championship_(golf)" title="United States Women&#39;s Open Championship (golf)">U.S. Women\'s Open</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Women%27s_British_Open" title="Women&#39;s British Open">Women\'s British Open</a> (which replaced the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Women%27s_Open" title="Canadian Women&#39;s Open">du Maurier Classic</a> as a major in 2001) and <a href="/wiki/The_Evian_Championship" title="The Evian Championship">The Evian Championship</a> (added as the fifth major in 2013). Only the last two are also recognised as majors by the <a href="/wiki/Ladies_European_Tour" title="Ladies European Tour">Ladies European Tour</a>. However, the significance of this is limited, as the LPGA is far more dominant in women\'s golf than the PGA Tour is in mainstream men\'s golf. For example, the <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a> has been known to use the U.S. definition of "women\'s majors" without qualifying it. Also, the <a href="/wiki/Ladies%27_Golf_Union" title="Ladies&#39; Golf Union">Ladies\' Golf Union</a>, the governing body for women\'s golf in Great Britain and Ireland, stated on its official website that the Women\'s British Open was "the only Women\'s Major to be played outside the U.S."<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> (this was before the elevation of The Evian Championship to major status). For many years, the Ladies European Tour tacitly acknowledged the dominance of the LPGA Tour by not scheduling any of its own events to conflict with the three LPGA majors played in the U.S., but that changed beginning in 2008, when the LET scheduled an event opposite the LPGA Championship. The second-richest women\'s tour, the <a href="/wiki/LPGA_of_Japan_Tour" title="LPGA of Japan Tour">LPGA of Japan Tour</a>, does not recognise any of the U.S. LPGA or European majors as it has its own set of majors (historically three, since 2008 four). However, these events attract little notice outside Japan.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Senior_major_championships">Senior major championships</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Senior_major_golf_championships" title="Senior major golf championships">Senior major golf championships</a></div>\n<p>Senior (aged fifty and over) men\'s golf does not have a globally agreed set of majors. The list of senior majors on the U.S.-based <a href="/wiki/PGA_Tour_Champions" title="PGA Tour Champions">PGA Tour Champions</a> has changed over the years, but always by expansion. PGA Tour Champions now recognises five majors: the <a href="/wiki/Senior_PGA_Championship" title="Senior PGA Championship">Senior PGA Championship</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Tradition" title="The Tradition">The Tradition</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Senior_Players_Championship" title="Senior Players Championship">Senior Players Championship</a>, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Senior_Open" class="mw-redirect" title="United States Senior Open">United States Senior Open</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Senior_Open_Championship" title="Senior Open Championship">The Senior (British) Open Championship</a>.\n</p><p>Of the five events, the Senior PGA is by far the oldest, having been founded in 1937. The other events all date from the 1980s, when senior golf became a commercial success as the first golf stars of the television era, such as <a href="/wiki/Arnold_Palmer" title="Arnold Palmer">Arnold Palmer</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gary_Player" title="Gary Player">Gary Player</a>, reached the relevant age. The Senior Open Championship was not recognised as a major by PGA Tour Champions until 2003. The <a href="/wiki/European_Senior_Tour" title="European Senior Tour">European Senior Tour</a> recognises only the Senior PGA and the two Senior Opens as majors. However, PGA Tour Champions is arguably more dominant in global senior golf than the U.S. LPGA is in global women\'s golf.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Olympic_Games">Olympic Games</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Golf_at_the_2016_Summer_Olympics" title="Golf at the 2016 Summer Olympics">Golf at the 2016 Summer Olympics</a></div>\n<p>After a 112-year absence from the Olympic Games, golf returned for the <a href="/wiki/Golf_at_the_2016_Summer_Olympics" title="Golf at the 2016 Summer Olympics">2016 Rio Games</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup>  41 different countries were represented by 120 athletes.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Controversy">Controversy</span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Women">Women</span></h3>\n<p>It wasn\'t until 1552 that the first woman golfer played the game. <a href="/wiki/Mary,_Queen_of_Scots" title="Mary, Queen of Scots">Mary Queen of Scots</a> commissioned <a href="/wiki/St_Andrews_Links" title="St Andrews Links">St. Andrew\'s Links</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> However, it wasn\'t until the 20th century that women were taken seriously and eventually broke the "Gentlemen Only, Ladies Forbidden" rule. Many men saw women as unfit to play the sport due to their lack of strength and ability.\n</p><p>In the United States, 1891 was a pivotal year for ladies golf because the <a href="/wiki/Shinnecock_Hills_Golf_Club" title="Shinnecock Hills Golf Club">Shinnecock Hills</a> nine-hole course was built in Southampton, New York, for women and was the first club to offer membership to women golfers. Four years later, in 1895, The U.S. Golf Association held the first Women\'s Amateur Championship tournament.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_57-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Just like professional golfer <a href="/wiki/Bobby_Jones_(golfer)" title="Bobby Jones (golfer)">Bobby Jones</a>, <a href="/wiki/Joyce_Wethered" title="Joyce Wethered">Joyce Wethered</a> was considered to be a star in the 1920s.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> Jones praised Wethered in 1930 after they had played an exhibition against each other. He doubted that there had ever been a better golfer, man or woman.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> However, Bobby Jones\' comment wasn\'t enough for others to change their views on women golfers.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Royal_Liverpool_Golf_Club" title="Royal Liverpool Golf Club">Royal Liverpool\'</a>s club refused entry of <a href="/wiki/Henry_Cotton_(golfer)" title="Henry Cotton (golfer)">Sir Henry Cotton</a>\'s wife into the clubhouse in the late 1940s. The secretary of the club released a statement saying, "No woman ever has entered the clubhouse and, praise God, no woman ever will."<sup id="cite_ref-:1_59-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> However, American golfer and all-around athlete, <a href="/wiki/Babe_Zaharias" class="mw-redirect" title="Babe Zaharias">Babe Zaharias</a> didn\'t have to enter the clubhouse. She was able to prove herself on the course, going on to become the first American to win the British Women\'s Amateur title in 1947. The following year she became the first woman to attempt to qualify for the <a href="/wiki/U.S._Open_(golf)" title="U.S. Open (golf)">U.S. Open</a>, but her application was rejected by the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Golf_Association" title="United States Golf Association">USGA</a>. They stated that the event was intended to be open to men only.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/LPGA" title="LPGA">Ladies Professional Golf Association</a> was formed in 1950 as a way to popularize the sport and provide competitive opportunities for golfers.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_59-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> The competitions were not the same for the men and women. It wasn\'t until 1972 that <a href="/wiki/United_States_Congress" title="United States Congress">U.S. Congress</a> passed the <a href="/wiki/Title_IX" title="Title IX">Title IX of the Education Amendments</a>. "No person in the United States shall, on the basis of sex, be excluded from participation in, be denied the benefits of, or be subject to discrimination under any education program or activities receiving Federal financial assistance."<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> American <a href="/wiki/Renee_Powell" title="Renee Powell">Renee Powell</a> moved to the UK in the 1970s to further her career, and became the first woman to play in a British men\'s tournament in 1977.<sup id="cite_ref-hennessy_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hennessy-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Today, women golfers are still fighting and working hard to have the same opportunities as men golfers. There is still a big pay gap in the USGA. The USGA has a long history of writing bigger checks to winners of the men\'s U.S. Open than the U.S. Women\'s Open.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="International_events">International events</span></h2>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Golf_at_the_Asian_Games" title="Golf at the Asian Games">Golf at the Asian Games</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Golf_at_the_Pan_American_Games" title="Golf at the Pan American Games">Golf at the Pan American Games</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Golf_at_the_Summer_Olympics" title="Golf at the Summer Olympics">Golf at the Summer Olympics</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Golf_at_the_Summer_Universiade" title="Golf at the Summer Universiade">Golf at the Summer Universiade</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Ryder_Cup" title="Ryder Cup">Ryder Cup</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Presidents_Cup" title="Presidents Cup">Presidents Cup</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Solheim_Cup" title="Solheim Cup">Solheim Cup</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/International_Crown" title="International Crown">International Crown</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Seve_Trophy" title="Seve Trophy">Seve Trophy</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/EurAsia_Cup" title="EurAsia Cup">EurAsia Cup</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Walker_Cup" title="Walker Cup">Walker Cup</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Curtis_Cup" title="Curtis Cup">Curtis Cup</a></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span></h2>\n<div role="navigation" aria-label="Portals"
